(Communication)
<span class="italic"><a title="Link to journal home page" href="https://doi.org/10.1039/1477-9234/2003">Dalton Trans.</a></span>, 2020, <strong>49</strong>, 4680-4684</div><h1 id="sect167"><span class="title_heading">Construction of the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C electrode with a one-dimensional porous hybrid structure as an advanced anode for sodium-ion batteries<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a></span></h1><p class="header_text">
      <span class="bold">
        
          
            Yakun 
            Tang
          
        
      </span>, 
      <span class="bold">
        
          
            Lang 
            Liu
          
        
      </span><span class="orcid"><a target="_blank" title="Select to open ORCID record for Lang&nbsp;Liu (orcid.org/0000-0002-8282-0859) in a new window" id="connect-orcid-link" href="http://orcid.org/0000-0002-8282-0859"><img id="orcid-id-logo" src="/content/NewImages/orcid_16x16.png" alt="ORCID logo"></a></span>*, 
      <span class="bold">

      <br><span class="italic">Key Laboratory of Energy Materials Chemistry, Ministry of Education; Institute of Applied Chemistry, Xinjiang University, Urumqi 830046, Xinjiang, China. E-mail: <a href="mailto:liulang@xju.edu.cn">liulang@xju.edu.cn</a>; <a href="mailto:llyhs1973@sina.com">llyhs1973@sina.com</a></span>
    </p><div id="art-admin"><span class="italic bold">Received 
      14th February 2020
    </span><span class="bold italic">, Accepted 10th March 2020</span></div><p class="bold italic">First published on 25th March 2020</p><hr><div class="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>The inferior electronic conductivity of NASICON materials leads to poor cyclability and rate capability, which severely inhibits their extensive development. Therefore, we have developed a one-dimensional (1D) hybrid electrode material that combines small NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles (550 nm) with a porous carbon matrix using a controllable solgel strategy. This unique design enables the electrode to possess good structural stability, superior charge transfer kinetics, and low polarization. The intimate combination between the nanoparticles and the porous carbon matrix can effectively facilitate Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>/e<small><sup></sup></small> transfer and accommodate volume variation during cycling. The construction of the new structure presented in this work will extend the applications of the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> system. Furthermore, the formed hybrid structure has potential to be a universal model for various electrode materials.</p></div><hr>
    
      <h2 id="sect239"><span class="a_heading">Introduction</span></h2>
      <span>Recently, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been widely used in portable electronic devices and hybrid electric vehicles;<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit1"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13</span></sup></a> meanwhile, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are undergoing rapid development. Thus, it is necessary to develop electrode materials with high capacity, excellent rate capability, and long cycle life.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit4"><sup><span class="sup_ref">4</span></sup></a> The working mechanism of SIBs is very similar to that of LIBs. Therefore, a number of methods have mimicked the successful material strategies used for LIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit5"><sup><span class="sup_ref">5,6</span></sup></a> In this regard, a series of promising SIB electrode materials have been discovered in the past decade. In terms of anode materials, however, commercialized graphite in LIBs exhibits extremely limited sodium storage properties because Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (1.16 ) has a larger ionic radius than Li<small><sup>+</sup></small> (0.90 ), which greatly hinders its reversible insertion into and extraction from the graphite anodes.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit7"><sup><span class="sup_ref">7</span></sup></a> Meanwhile, the drastic volume changes accompanying the alloying or transition metal compounds lead to structural degradation and then a rapid capacity decay.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit8"><sup><span class="sup_ref">8,9</span></sup></a> Therefore, the lack of suitable intercalation anode materials is a huge limitation for advanced SIB systems.</span>
      <p class="otherpara">Nowadays, NASICON materials have been widely applied in SIBs because of the open stable 3D framework and nearly unchanged volume during the charge and discharge processes.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit10"><sup><span class="sup_ref">10</span></sup></a> Among them, NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> has received great attention by virtue of its environmental friendliness and low cost.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit11"><sup><span class="sup_ref">11</span></sup></a> Nevertheless, the rate capability and cycling stability of NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> are severely limited by the sluggish kinetics of the electrons. However, the electron transport kinetics of NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> has been improved by constructing a composite of nanostructured NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> with conductive carbon (thin carbon coating, loading on CNTs, and graphene wrapping).<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit12"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1214</span></sup></a> These studies have doubtlessly reported better NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>-based electrode materials. It is noteworthy that the fabrication of 1D nanostructured electrode materials has additional advantages including shortened ion diffusion paths, facile strain relaxation, and large surface-to-volume ratios.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15,16</span></sup></a> However, the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> particles usually have a large size because of the rapid precipitation between Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small> and HPO<small><sub>4</sub></small><small><sup>2</sup></small>/H<small><sub>2</sub></small>PO<small><sub>4</sub></small><small><sup></sup></small>/PO<small><sub>4</sub></small><small><sup>3</sup></small>, and the unsatisfactory contact between NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> and the 1D carbon matrix limits the improvement in electrochemical performance.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Fortunately, an electrospinning technique can be feasibly used to fabricate 1D nanostructures, in which the active material and carbon can contact favorably.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit17"><sup><span class="sup_ref">17,18</span></sup></a> Therefore, some researchers have reported studies on the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers. Li <span class="italic">et al.</span> synthesized NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C composite nanofibers, which exhibited a reversible capacity of 97 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 665 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 500 cycles.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit19"><sup><span class="sup_ref">19</span></sup></a> Wei <span class="italic">et al.</span> prepared NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C hierarchical porous nanofibers with excellent rate capability.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit20"><sup><span class="sup_ref">20</span></sup></a> Nevertheless, the specific capacity of the above-mentioned electrode materials is still unsatisfactory due to the large size and poor dispersity of the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> particles. Meanwhile, the pre-operational control condition (temperature, voltage, humidity, <span class="italic">etc.</span>) of the electrospinning technique is tedious. Hence, there is an urgent need to develop a novel technique for constructing well-structured 1D NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C electrode materials.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Exhilaratingly, we have successfully synthesized Ti-based compound/C hybrids with a 1D nanostructure using a modified solgel method.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit21"><sup><span class="sup_ref">21,22</span></sup></a> The hybrid electrodes composed of nanosized homodisperse active materials and conductive porous carbon have superior electrochemical performance. In our proof-of-concept study, we legitimately designed and synthesized NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C hybrid nanotubes by a solgel method and a subsequent calcination process, in which nanoparticles (550 nm) were uniformly embedded within the porous carbon matrix. The formation process of the hybrid is illustrated in <a title="Select to navigate to scheme" href="#imgsch1">Scheme 1</a>. First, tetrabutyltitanate (TBT) was adsorbed onto the walls of sulfonated polymer nanotubes (SPNTs). Then, the above-mentioned mixture was stirred at 60 C in an ethanol solution containing Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>3</sub></small> and P<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>5</sub></small> to form a precursor. Finally, 1D hybrids were obtained through post-annealing treatment (denoted as NTP). The NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles are embedded in the porous carbon matrix, which improves the electrical contact. Consequently, NTP delivered the combined advantage of large capacity (129 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 150 cycles), high rate performance, and long-term cycling stability (55.5 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 3000 cycles).</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgsch1"><a href="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-s1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0dt00548g-s1.tif" src="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-s1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Scheme 1 </b> <span id="sch1"><span class="graphic_title">Schematic illustration of the preparation of NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C 1D porous hybrids.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
    
    
      <h2 id="sect329"><span class="a_heading">Experimental section</span></h2>
      
        <h3 id="sect331"><span class="b_heading">Materials</span></h3>
        <span>All the reagents were AR grade and provided by commercial suppliers. The sulfonated polymer nanotubes (SPNTs) were obtained according to our previously reported method.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit23"><sup><span class="sup_ref">23</span></sup></a></span>
      
      
        <h3 id="sect335"><span class="b_heading">Synthesis of NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C porous hybrid nanotubes</span></h3>
        <span>First, 70 mg of SPNTs were dispersed in 4 mL of ethanol under ultrasonication for 30 min. Second, tetrabutyltitanate (TBT, 1.7 g) was added to the mixture and stirred for 12 h at an ambient temperature. Third, 8 mL ethanol solution containing Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>3</sub></small> (0.159 g) and P<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>5</sub></small> (0.596 g) was added into the above system and stirred for 6 h at 60 C. After centrifugation, the residue was carefully collected and wiped with a tissue paper. The obtained precursor was dried in air at 80 C for 12 h. Finally, the as-synthesized precursor was calcined at 900 C for 6 h in N<small><sub>2</sub></small> (heating rate: 5 C min<small><sup>1</sup></small>) to obtain NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C porous hybrid nanotubes (denoted as NTP).</span>
      
      
        <h3 id="sect350"><span class="b_heading">Characterization</span></h3>
        <span>Material characterization and electrochemical tests were carried out according to our previous methods.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit24"><sup><span class="sup_ref">24</span></sup></a></span>
      
    
    
      <h2 id="sect354"><span class="a_heading">Results and discussion</span></h2>
      <span>The X-ray diffraction pattern of NTP is shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1a</a>; all the characteristic diffraction peaks of the sample can be indexed to well-crystalline NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> with a rhombohedral structure (JCPDS card no. 33-1296). No diffraction peaks attributed to the carbon matrix can be observed because of the amorphous structure.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit21"><sup><span class="sup_ref">21</span></sup></a> Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) of NTP was carried out from 25 to 800 C in air (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1b</a>). The weight loss below 300 C is related to the evaporation of water. The mass loss from 300 to 500 C can be ascribed to the combustion of the carbon matrix. The percentage of carbon in NTP was estimated to be 18.1%. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1c</a> displays the N<small><sub>2</sub></small> adsorptiondesorption curves. The BrunauerEmmettTeller surface area of NTP was 194.4 m<small><sup>2</sup></small> g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Obviously, NTP possessed a mesoporous structure, and the size distribution ranged from 2 to 30 nm (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1d</a>). Meanwhile, the larger surface area of NTP resulted from the porous carbon matrix with abundant micropores (12 nm) and the perfect 1D hybrid nanostructure.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit21"><sup><span class="sup_ref">21</span></sup></a> These pores and large surface area will result in superior Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> transfer from the electrode.</span>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig1"><a href="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-f1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0dt00548g-f1.tif" src="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-f1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 1 </b> <span id="fig1"><span class="graphic_title">XRD pattern, (a) TGA curve (b), N<small><sub>2</sub></small> adsorptiondesorption isotherm (c), and pore size distribution (d) of NTP.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">Field emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM), transmission electron microscopy (TEM), and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) provided details regarding the morphological characteristics of NTP (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2</a>). <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2a</a> shows the SEM image of NTP, revealing the 1D morphology with a diameter of 100120 nm. No obvious agglomerated particles were observed. However, the surface of NTP had some bulges. To further identify the clear morphology of the sample, the TEM images of NTP are given in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2b and c</a>. The hybrid possesses a perfect bamboo-like shape; the lighter and darker colors of the hybrid represent the carbon matrix and NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles, respectively. Obviously, the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles with different size distributions (550 nm) are well embedded in the 1D carbon nanotubes. Meanwhile, the major NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles are half-embedded in the wall of the nanotubes, leading to bulges on the surface of NTP. The formation of the embedded structure can be due to the presence of the Ti-based gel precursor in the walls of SPNTs. In addition, the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles have uniform dispersion and small size due to the weak precipitation between Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small> and HPO<small><sub>4</sub></small><small><sup>2</sup></small>/H<small><sub>2</sub></small>PO<small><sub>4</sub></small><small><sup></sup></small>/PO<small><sub>4</sub></small><small><sup>3</sup></small> because the main ingredient of the ionic ethanol solution containing P<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>5</sub></small> can form organic phosphate.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">25</span></sup></a></p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig2"><a href="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-f2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0dt00548g-f2.tif" src="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-f2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 2 </b> <span id="fig2"><span class="graphic_title">SEM (a), TEM (b and c), and HRTEM images (d) of NTP; EDS mappings of (e) C, (f) P, (g) Na, and (h) Ti in NTP.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The HRTEM image shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2d</a> indicates the disordered thin layers of carbon around the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles (darker color). Inside the particles, an indistinct lattice fringe of 0.276 nm is observed, corresponding to the interplanar spacing of the (116) plane for the rhombohedral lattice (Fig. S1<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26</span></sup></a> The presence of the 3D carbon matrix not only inhibits the agglomeration but also prevents the growth of the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> particles. According to the elemental mappings shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2eh</a>, the C, P, Na, and Ti elements are uniformly distributed in NTP. The SEM image (NTP) of ESD mappings is shown in the ESI (Fig. S2<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The combination of the preparation of dispersive small nanoparticles and the introduction of a 3D carbon matrix with a porous structure greatly shortens the transfer pathway of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> and improves the electronic conductivity.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The electrochemical performance of NTP was tested between 0.01 and 3 V. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3a</a> displays the cyclic voltammetry (CV) profiles of NTP in the initial three cycles at 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The redox pairs at 2.05/2.22 V and 0.35/0.51 V can be assigned to the mutual transformation of Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small> and Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>  Ti<small><sup>2+</sup></small>, respectively, which is consistent with a previous report.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26</span></sup></a> An irreversible cathodic peak at about 1.1 V is observed in the first cycle owing to the decomposition of the electrolyte to form a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27</span></sup></a> Compared with most reported NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>-based electrodes, NTP shows well-defined peaks and smaller potential interval,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit28"><sup><span class="sup_ref">28,29</span></sup></a> which demonstrates the lower polarization. The diffusion/migration barrier of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> insertion was reduced due to the porous carbon matrix and the well-dispersed nanoparticles.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0dt00548g-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2020/DT/d0dt00548g/d0dt00548g-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">CV curves at 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small> (a), GCD curves at 0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (b), cycle performances at 0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, and 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (c), rate performance (d) and cycle performance at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (e) of NTP.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The lowest pair at about 0 V is caused by the insertion of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> in amorphous carbon.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27</span></sup></a> Moreover, the overlap of the subsequent CV curves indicates high reversibility of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> in NTP. The typical galvanostatic chargedischarge (GCD) profiles of the NTP electrode at 0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> are shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3b</a>. Two voltage plateaus at about 2.1 and 0.5 V in the 1st GCD profiles are observed, which are similar to that in the CV profiles. The formed SEI layer is confirmed by the plateau at 1.1 V in the initial GCD profile and the low coulombic efficiency (CE) of 56.7%. After the 2nd cycle, all the GCD profiles are superimposed on each other with a high discharge capacity over 160 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Moreover, a good CE over 97% was obtained after the 10th cycle.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The cycling behaviors of NTP at different current densities are given in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3c</a>. The electrodes deliver the initial capacities of 357.4, 286.3, and 225.2 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, and 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. After 150 cycles, the electrode retains a high capacity of 129 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Notably, it maintains high reversible capacities of 102.1 and 93.7 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 5 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 150 cycles, respectively, which indicates excellent cycling stability and rate capability. Meanwhile, the results for the coulombic efficiency of the cycled cells under the above-mentioned different rates are given in the ESI (Fig. S3<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The rate cycling performance of the NTP electrode was further tested upon increasing the current density from 0.1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> to 6 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3d</a>); the electrode delivered a high capacity of 88.5 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 6 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. When the current density returned to 0.1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the reversible capacity rapidly returned to the original value once more, demonstrating its good cycling stability and flexible structure. In addition, to further demonstrate the cycling stability of NTP, the electrode was cycled at 10 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3e</a>). A long lifespan of 3000 cycles was realized with a high CE of 100% as well as a desirable capacity of 55.5 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Moreover, NTP exhibited superior electrochemical performance than the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>-based materials tested between 0.01 and 3 V reported in the open literature;<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26,30,31</span></sup></a> this fully demonstrates that the construction of a 1D hybrid structure can be used to promote the electrochemical performance. The aggregation and pulverization of the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles were effectively prevented, which could accommodate the volume change during the electrochemical reaction and also shorten the diffusion path of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> and electrons. Meanwhile, the NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles wrapped with a porous carbon matrix could provide fast electronic and ionic transport. Also, the carbon skeleton improved the electrical conductivity of NTP and further prevented the structure from collapsing during long cycling. In addition, the hierarchical pore structure of NTP increased the surface area between the electrodes and the electrolytes and abundant active sites, which endowed the electrodes with high capacitive contribution.</p>
    
    
      <h2 id="sect477"><span class="a_heading">Conclusions</span></h2>
      <span>In summary, we have synthesized 1D porous hybrid nanotubes with the synergistic effect of NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles and porous carbon matrix as a promising electrode for SIBs. This novel architecture endowed the electrode with excellent electrochemical performance in terms of high capacity, excellent rate capability, and long cycle life. In the structure, the ion/electron transfer and structural stability significantly improved during the electrochemical reaction. Also, the small NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles augmented the active sites for Na<small><sup>+</sup></small>. Moreover, owing to the rational combination of the merits of the porous structure and carbon matrix, high electrical conductivity was achieved. The volume expansion during cycling was buffered by the elastic carbon matrix. Thus, besides the attractive electrochemical performance achieved here, this study highlights the importance of the synergistic effect of 1D porous hybrid structures in rechargeable batteries.</span>
